Alexandre Ghiti

6 items
Patches Submitted (2)
Last comment 2026-05-18 [PATCH] mm: memcontrol: propagate NMI slab stats to memcg vmstats Neutral LLM

This patch fixes a bug in the memcontrol code where NMI slab stats are not propagated to memcg vmstats, leading to inconsistent statistics. The fix involves modifying the flush_nmi_stats function to update both per-node lruvec_stats and memcg-level vmstats.

1 reviewer comment — 0 participants
0 participants
Johannes Weiner Acked-by Positive LLM
Acked the patch without raising any concerns.
Show original comment 
On Mon, May 18, 2026 at 10:28:19AM +0200, Alexandre Ghiti wrote:
> flush_nmi_stats() drains per-node NMI slab atomics into the per-node
> lruvec_stats, but does not propagate them to the memcg-level vmstats.
> 
> For non NMI case, account_slab_nmi_safe() calls mod_memcg_lruvec_state()
> which updates both per-node lruvec_stats and memcg-level vmstats, so
> flush_nmi_stats() needs to flush to per-node lruvec_stats as well as
> memcg-level vmstats.
> 
> So fix this by flushing to the memcg-level vmstats for NMI too.
> 
> Fixes: 940b01fc8dc1 ("memcg: nmi safe memcg stats for specific archs")
> Cc: stable@vger.kernel.org
> Acked-by: Shakeel Butt <shakeel.butt@linux.dev>
> Signed-off-by: Alexandre Ghiti <alex@ghiti.fr>

Acked-by: Johannes Weiner <hannes@cmpxchg.org>
Ongoing Submitted 2026-05-11 Last comment 2026-05-18 ⏱ No recent activity [PATCH 0/8] per-memcg-per-node kmem accounting 8 patches
Show 8 individual patches
  • [1/8] mm: memcontrol: propagate NMI slab stats to memcg vmstats Neutral Submitted 2026-05-11Last comment 2026-05-12 Shakeel Butt
  • [2/8] mm: percpu: charge obj_exts allocation with __GFP_ACCOUNT Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [3/8] mm: percpu: Split memcg charging and kmem accounting Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [4/8] mm: memcontrol: track MEMCG_KMEM per NUMA node Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [5/8] mm: memcontrol: per-node kmem accounting for page charges Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [6/8] mm: slab: per-node kmem accounting for slab Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [7/8] mm: percpu: per-node kmem accounting using local credit Submitted 2026-05-11
  • [8/8] mm: zswap: per-node kmem accounting for zswap/zsmalloc Submitted 2026-05-11
Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch series introduces per-memcg-per-node kernel memory accounting to associate memcg and physical memory usage. It builds on recent changes to obj_cgroup, which ties object groups to their NUMA node. The patches split kmem charging and accounting for percpu allocations, and convert other kmem users such as slab and zswap to use the new per-node accounting. This allows for more accurate tracking of kernel memory usage at a per-node level.

2 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants

Joshua Hahn ↳ replying to Alexandre Ghiti Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer Joshua Hahn expressed concerns about the performance impact of the patch, specifically suggesting that expensive operations would benefit from benchmarking to demonstrate kernel allocation overhead. Reviewer Joshua Hahn expressed concerns about the performance implications of splitting obj_cgroup to be per-node, which would invalidate the obj_stock cache and lead to increased atomic operations. He also questioned the need for iterating over num_possible_cpus() x pages_per_alloc.
Show original comment 
Hello Alex,

Thank you for your work!

Overall I think the direction makes sense to me. Pre-overcharging makes sense to
me as an approach, we would much rather overaccount than underaccount and
later have to breach limits.

I do have some concerns on performance, though. Namely, I think there are
some expensive operations that I think would benefit from some performane
benchmarking with this patch added (maybe some simple microbenchmarks that
demonstrates kernel allocation overhead could be useful).

---

to do with iterating over num_possible_cpus() x pages_per_alloc, which
doesn't seem trivial to me.

Another concern that I see is the stock credit system. Maybe we could be
bypassing the stock check leading to more time spent doing the atomic
operations.

obj_stock caches a single obj_cgroup, which means that if we split the objcg
to be per-node (in patch 6), then the obj_stock basically gets invalidated
every operation since we iterate over more objcgs (even though we are in
the same logical objcg). Maybe I'm missing something?

I haven't taken a deep look at the implementation details but just wanted to
raise some high level items that I noticed. Of course, all of these concerns
are just theoretical, if you can show that the performance delta is not
noticable then all of my concerns don't matter.

I also want to talk more about the local credit system but let's first see
what the numbers are first.

Thanks again, Alex. And I really like patch 2 because it is a solution to
a problem that I ran into in my percpu tracking series that I couldn't think
of before! Thank you for solving my problem too : -)

Have a great day!
Joshua

Last comment 2026-05-20 Re: [PATCH 0/8] per-memcg-per-node kmem accounting Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch series aims to improve kmem accounting by making it per-memcg-per-node, which is a more accurate and efficient way of tracking memory usage. The current implementation has been shown to have a significant performance regression, and this series attempts to address that issue. The approach taken involves reworking the objcg split introduced in a previous commit to reduce overhead.

1 reviewer comment — 0 participants
0 participants
Joshua Hahn ↳ replying to Alexandre Ghiti Inline Review Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer questioned which atomic operations could be bypassed, indicating a lack of understanding about the patch's intent and requesting clarification. reviewer noted that the patch may incur extra work in certain scenarios where obj_cgroup stock and local credit 'stock' are out of sync, specifically in the stock refill path and pcpu_memcg_post_alloc_hook, and suggested a potential optimization to precharge all pages before performing atomic operations Reviewer questioned the need for atomic operations to be bypassed in certain scenarios and asked for clarification on which specific operations could be optimized.
Show original comment 
Hi Alex,

That sounds great with me : -) Looking forward to the numbers!

---

So in my initial scan of the patch 7 I had a concern that if we have a nested
stock system (obj_cgroup stock and local credit "stock"), then we could
incur more work if these are out of sync; do extra work in the stock refill
path in obj_cgroup_precharge, and then do extra work on top in the loop
within the pcpu_memcg_post_alloc_hook (obj_cgroup_account_kmem does the
charging atomically I think).

So what I mean is, I'm not sure what the "size" is typically for
pcpu_memcg_post_alloc_hook. But it might be a worthwhile optimization to
do precharge all the pages, then for each cpu iterate over the pages to
figure out how many pages are used per nid (doing just math, not actually
doing the atomic adds), and then outside both of these loops just iterate
over every nid_objcg once to perform the atomic operation.

Maybe this is needed or not (depending on how big "size" typically is
and whether we go from doing O(1000) atomic adds --> O(10) or some
big reduction, but I just wanted to toss it out there as something that
could potentially be expensive.

---

Sounds like a great idea! Thanks again Alex, have a great day! : -)
Joshua

Ongoing Submitted 2026-05-13 Last comment 2026-05-18 ⏱ No recent activity [PATCH 2/2] btrfs: test qgroup deletion races with squota writes Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch adds four test cases to the Btrfs file system to detect and prevent various race conditions that can occur when deleting a qgroup (quota group) while writing quotas. The tests cover scenarios where an extent's owner reference outlives its subvolume, leading to potential underflows or transaction aborts. The patch aims to ensure correct quota accounting by rejecting qgroup deletion requests in these situations.

Reviews Given (8)
Last comment 2026-05-21 Re: [PATCH v2 2/6] btrfs: add delayed ordered extent support Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch introduces a new concept of 'delayed ordered extent' in Btrfs, which is a range of file extents without submitted I/O or space allocation. The existing code for finishing one ordered extent can be reused on the children of this delayed OE, with only minor modifications. The idea is to split the concepts of ordered extent and its parent into two separate entities: one representing the range of file extents in the rb-tree, and the other representing the I/O operations. This change simplifies the code and reduces the need for special handling of parent-child relationships between OEs.

2 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Qu Wenruo ↳ replying to Boris Burkov Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer noted that classic OEs are not directly equivalent to bio submissions, citing large OE sizes and limited bio size as reasons for multiple smaller bios being submitted for a single OE. Reviewer suggested migrating non-compressed writes into layer OEs or split OEs to handle truncation cases better, but noted that implementing this would require significant extra work to simplify the structure and remove unnecessary members from parent OEs. Reviewer Qu Wenruo expressed agreement with Boris's proposed change to split ordered extent concepts into two types: one representing a range of file and another for I/O, suggesting that this would simplify the code and eliminate conditional logic.
Show original comment 
To be a little strict, the classic OE is not 1:1 with bio submitted.

The truth is, we can have super large OE, up to 128MIB. But our bio can 
only be as large as 1MiB for the worst cases.
Thus we will have a lot of smaller bios submitted for the same OE.

---

I have a similar idea for the long run, to migrate the non-compressed 
writes into the layer OEs (or split OEs), so that we can handle the 
truncation cases better, without allocating a larger than needed data 
extent.

However going all in on layered OEs will need quite some extra work in 
simplifying the structure, a lot of members in the parent OE is no 
longer required and should be simplified for layered OE solution.

---

If we're fine with the current layered OE solution, I'm totally fine 
going that path, migrating all writes to layered OE, and simplify the 
structure.

Thanks,
Qu

Re: [PATCH v2 2/6] btrfs: add delayed ordered extent support Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies
Last comment 2026-05-21 Re: [PATCH v2 1/6] btrfs: add skeleton for delayed btrfs bio Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch introduces a new concept of 'delayed ordered extent' in Btrfs, which is a range of file extents without submitted I/O or space allocation. The existing code for finishing one ordered extent can be reused on the children of this delayed OE, with only minor modifications. The idea is to split the concepts of ordered extent and its parent into two separate entities: one representing the range of file extents in the rb-tree, and the other representing the I/O operations. This change simplifies the code and reduces the need for special handling of parent-child relationships between OEs.

1 reviewer comment — 0 participants
0 participants
Qu Wenruo ↳ replying to Boris Burkov Inline Review Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer Qu Wenruo analyzed the callers of btrfs_get_extent() and found that they all have different kinds of protection against EXTENT_MAP_DELAYED, including checks for last byte, writeback or wait ordered extents, extra handling before calling btrfs_get_extent(), exact submit path checking, and only caring about holes/prealloc. The reviewer noted that since the delayed OE is only for writeback, the folio is always uptodate. Reviewer Qu Wenruo expressed concern that using a false bbio as an async placeholder may not be necessary for some callers of btrfs_get_extent() to handle delayed extents, and suggested reusing the same submission code for both real and delayed bio submissions. Reviewer questioned the purpose of using a false bbio as an async placeholder in btrfs_get_extent(), noting that it serves a specific objective beyond mere convenience, and requested clarification on its importance.

I checked all btrfs_get_extent() callers, they have all different kinds 
of protection:

- Check against EXTENT_MAP_LAST_BYTE

- Have writeback or wait ordered extents for the range
   Including:
   * Direct IO

   In our case, since the delayed OE is only for writeback, the
   folio is always uptodate.

- Callers only care about holes/prealloc

Last comment 2026-05-18 [PATCH v3 0/4] cleanup: Remove NULL check from unconditional guards Neutral LLM

This patch series aims to remove dead NULL checks from unconditional guard destructors in the Linux kernel. The patches prepare guards that handle NULL, add __nonnull() attributes for compile-time enforcement, and finally remove the unnecessary checks.

1 reviewer comment — 0 participants
0 participants
Miguel Ojeda ↳ replying to Dmitry Ilvokhin Reviewed-by Neutral LLM
Identified a discrepancy in the documentation links for __nonnull() attributes and suggested correcting them. Also, pointed out that the attribute does not prevent NULL pointers from being passed.
Show original comment 
On Mon, May 18, 2026 at 5:22 PM Dmitry Ilvokhin <d@ilvokhin.com> wrote:
>
> Add __nonnull() to unconditional guard constructors so the compiler
> verifies at each call site that NULL is never passed:

> This provides automated, compiler-enforced verification that no
> unconditional guard constructor receives NULL.

I wouldn't say "verify", since the compiler does a best-effort here
with the information it has statically.

In other words, the attribute does not prevent NULL pointers to be passed.

> + *   gcc: https://gcc.gnu.org/onlinedocs/gcc/Common-Function-Attributes.html#index-nonnull-function-attribute

Hmm... It appears GCC has changed the docs in commit 6e3c137f5dbb
("doc: Merge function, variable, type, and statement attribute
sections [PR88472]"), dropping the per-kind attribute pages.

So the right link would need to be now:

  https://gcc.gnu.org/onlinedocs/gcc/Common-Attributes.html#index-nonnull

I will need to send a patch to fix the other links.

> + * clang: https://clang.llvm.org/docs/AttributeReference.html#nonnull

I think this link goes to `_Nonnull` -- the GNU one is instead:

  https://clang.llvm.org/docs/AttributeReference.html#id10

(I don't love the numeric IDs, though, since they break, so I think it
is fine either way -- the `_Nonnull` is fairly close to the one we
want and I hope that one doesn't break)

> + */
> +#define __nonnull(x...)                        __attribute__((__nonnull__(x)))

This is indeed available for a long time, and we already use it
elsewhere in the kernel tree (which would be nice to clean up
separately).

If you don't mind, please place it before `__nonstring__` (the file is
meant to be sorted by the actual attribute name -- there are a few
instances where this is not the case anymore, which I will eventually
clean up)

Thanks!

Cheers,
Miguel

Last comment 2026-05-18 [PATCH v3 1/4] nvdimm: Convert nvdimm_bus guard to class Neutral LLM

This patch converts the nvdimm_bus guard from a DEFINE_GUARD() to a class-based implementation using DEFINE_CLASS() and DEFINE_CLASS_IS_GUARD(). This change is necessary because the current implementation accepts NULL values, which will cause a compile error when the constructor is made __nonnull(). The patch makes no functional changes.

Last comment 2026-05-18 [PATCH v3 3/4] cleanup: Annotate guard constructors with __nonnull() Neutral LLM

This patch series aims to annotate guard constructors in the Linux kernel with __nonnull() attribute, ensuring that compilers verify at each call site that NULL is not passed to these constructors. The annotation involves re-declaring the constructor with __nonnull() or directly annotating it. This provides automated verification of unconditional guard constructors receiving NULL.

Last comment 2026-05-18 [PATCH] mm/page_alloc: fix defrag_mode for non-reclaimable allocations Neutral LLM

The patch addresses an issue where defrag_mode in the page allocator fails to handle non-reclaimable allocations, leading to SLUB allocation failures under network-heavy workloads. It does this by clearing ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT and retrying the allocation when direct reclaim is not possible.

1 reviewer comment — 0 participants
0 participants
Andrew Morton ↳ replying to Dmitry Ilvokhin Neutral LLM
Raised a question about the potential impact of the change on concurrent cpuset or zonelist alterations, and also pointed out a possible conflict with a later comment in the code.
Show original comment 
On Mon, 18 May 2026 16:37:36 +0000 Dmitry Ilvokhin <d@ilvokhin.com> wrote:

> When defrag_mode is enabled, ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT is enforced to prevent
> migratetype fallbacks and keep pageblocks clean. The allocator relies on
> reclaim and compaction to free pages of the correct type before allowing
> fallback as a last resort.
> 
> However, non-reclaimable allocations such as GFP_ATOMIC cannot invoke
> direct reclaim or compaction. With defrag_mode=1, these allocations hit
> the !can_direct_reclaim bailout in __alloc_pages_slowpath() with
> ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT still set, and fail without ever attempting a fallback.
> 
> This causes a large number of SLUB allocation failures for
> skbuff_head_cache under network-heavy workloads, despite free memory
> being available in other migratetype freelists.
> 
> Clear ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT and retry before giving up on allocations that
> cannot reclaim, following the same pattern used after reclaim/compaction
> exhaustion later in the slowpath.

Thanks.  Sashiko asked a couple of things:

	https://sashiko.dev/#/patchset/20260518163736.173910-1-d@ilvokhin.com

I'm not sure what to make of the first one - we aren't holding any locks
in there which prevent concurrent cpuset or zonelist alterations
anyway (?).

But your change might violate the later comment `No "goto retry;" can be
placed above this check * unless it can execute just once'?
Signals: QUESTION
[PATCH v2] mm/page_alloc: fix defrag_mode for non-reclaimable allocations Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies

This patch fixes a problem in the Linux kernel's page allocation system where non-reclaimable allocations, such as those made with GFP_ATOMIC, fail when defrag_mode is enabled. The issue arises because these allocations cannot invoke direct reclaim or compaction, which are necessary for defrag_mode to work correctly. To fix this, the patch clears the ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT flag and retries the allocation if it requests kswapd reclaim but cannot do direct reclaim itself. This change allows non-reclaimable allocations to fall back to other migration types when defrag_mode is enabled, preventing a large number of SLUB allocation failures under network-heavy workloads.

[PATCH v4 1/4] nvdimm: Convert nvdimm_bus guard to class Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies

This patch converts the nvdimm_bus guard from using DEFINE_GUARD() to a combination of DEFINE_CLASS() and DEFINE_CLASS_IS_GUARD(). This change is necessary because the upcoming removal of NULL checks in DEFINE_GUARD() constructors would cause a compile error for nvdimm_bus, which can pass NULL. The conversion does not introduce any functional changes.

[PATCH v4 2/4] genirq: Move NULL check into irqdesc_lock guard unlock expression Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies

This patch moves a NULL check from the __DEFINE_UNLOCK_GUARD macro to the call site of irqdesc_lock's unlock expression, making the handling of NULL locks explicit and preparing for future removal of the NULL check from the macro.

[PATCH v4 3/4] cleanup: Annotate guard constructors with __nonnull() Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies

This patch annotates guard constructors in the Linux kernel with __nonnull() to ensure that compilers warn when NULL is statically known to be passed as an argument. The annotation is applied to DEFINE_GUARD() and __DEFINE_LOCK_GUARD_1(), while DEFINE_LOCK_GUARD_0() remains unchanged since its constructor does not take a pointer argument. The __nonnull() macro is defined in compiler_attributes.h, following the existing convention for attribute wrappers.

[PATCH v4 4/4] cleanup: Remove NULL check from unconditional guards Neutral llm-chunked-no-replies

This patch removes unnecessary NULL checks from unconditional guards in the Linux kernel. The checks were dead code because the guards guarantee a non-NULL lock pointer at destructor time. The patch affects several macros, including DEFINE_GUARD(), DEFINE_LOCK_GUARD_1(), and DEFINE_LOCK_GUARD_0(). It also fixes a few specific instances where the NULL check was not being used correctly. The changes are verified to have no performance impact, with a negligible reduction in code size.

> > > 
> > > However, non-reclaimable allocations such as GFP_ATOMIC cannot invoke
> > > direct reclaim or compaction. With defrag_mode=1, these allocations hit
> > > the !can_direct_reclaim bailout in __alloc_pages_slowpath() with
> > > ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT still set, and fail without ever attempting a fallback.
> > > 
> > > This causes a large number of SLUB allocation failures for
> > > skbuff_head_cache under network-heavy workloads, despite free memory
> > > being available in other migratetype freelists.
> > > 
> > > Clear ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT and retry before giving up on allocations that
> > > cannot reclaim, following the same pattern used after reclaim/compaction
> > > exhaustion later in the slowpath.
> > 
> > Thanks.  Sashiko asked a couple of things:
> > 
> > 	https://sashiko.dev/#/patchset/20260518163736.173910-1-d@ilvokhin.com
> > 
> > I'm not sure what to make of the first one - we aren't holding any locks
> > in there which prevent concurrent cpuset or zonelist alterations
> > anyway (?).
> > 
> > But your change might violate the later comment `No "goto retry;" can be
> > placed above this check * unless it can execute just once'?
> 
> Thanks for taking a look, Andrew.
> 
> Goto retry can execute at most once, since ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT is cleared
> before the jump, so on the next iteration the condition is false and we
> fall through to goto nopage. This is the similar to the existing
> can_retry_reserves path.

Yes, it's just a one-off retry with relaxed fragmentation rules, no
need to re-evaluate the cpuset. So this looks fine to me.

> Just for the sake of keeping everything in one place. Another point
> Sashiko raised.
> 
> "Will allocations hitting this PF_MEMALLOC check, or the __GFP_NORETRY check
> further down in the function, still fail prematurely under defrag_mode=1?
> Because these terminal error paths also jump directly to the nopage label,
> they skip the normal ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT clearing at the bottom of the slowpath.
> Should we also clear ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT and retry for these paths so they are
> allowed to fall back rather than failing outright?"
> 
> I think by the time we reach the PF_MEMALLOC check, ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT has
> already been cleared, since we set only ALLOC_NO_WATERMARKS and
> ALLOC_KSWAPD in reserve_flags, when PF_MEMALLOC is set.

Yes, that's correct. alloc_flags gets overwritten, losing NOFRAGMENT,
for privileged requests. And then we retry with that already.

> For GFP_NORETRY, we can do direct reclaim (compared to GFP_ATOMIC case),
> so we either succeed or not, we don't need another round.

This is an interesting question.

GFP_NORETRY can reclaim and compact once, yes, but ALLOC_NOFRAGMENT is
still a higher bar, increasing the likelihood of failure.

However, unlike GFP_ATOMIC, GFP_NORETRY are usually speculative
allocations with reasonable fallback options (like slub's optimistic
higher order requests).

The idea behind defrag_mode is to not fragment until the alternative
is OOM. For GFP_ATOMIC, failing is an OOM-like event. For the other
nopage cases, it's more about "my favorite thing isn't available".

So I'd say let's fix GFP_ATOMIC and leave the other cases alone unless
somebody specifically brings it up as an issue.

However, there is one catch: GFP_ATOMIC is not its own flag. You're
gating on can_direct_reclaim which is also true for optimistic things
like mTHP allocations (GFP_TRANSHUGE_LIGHT e.g.). We don't want to
fragment for those, either.

So I think you'd want to check at least if __GFP_KSWAPD_RECLAIM is set
(which it is for GFP_ATOMIC) to decide between fragmenting and
failing. If the caller doesn't even set that, it's a good indicator
that they're purely speculative, and failing is the better option.

With that,

Acked-by: Johannes Weiner <hannes@cmpxchg.org>
Signals: NEEDS_WORK

Last comment 2026-05-21 [PATCH] nfsd: fix posix_acl leak and ignored error in nfsd4_create_file Neutral LLM

This patch fixes two bugs in the NFSv4 server's ACL handling code: a posix_acl leak and an ignored error in nfsd4_create_file(). The leaks occur when start_creating() fails after populating ACL attributes, causing the posix_acl allocations to be lost. The ignored error is due to silently discarding the return value of nfsd4_acl_to_attr(), which should reject unsupported ACE types. The patch addresses these issues by capturing the return value and changing early error paths to jump to out instead of out_write.

Last comment 2026-05-22 [PATCH] nfsd: reset write verifier on deferred writeback errors Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch fixes a bug in the NFS server where deferred writeback errors were not properly handled, leading to silent data loss. The issue arises when clients hold UNSTABLE write data under the current verifier and then COMMIT, only to receive the unchanged verifier back and conclude their data is durable. To fix this, the patch adds calls to commit_reset_write_verifier() at two error sites in nfsd_vfs_write() and nfsd_commit(), ensuring that the server's write verifier is properly rotated on deferred writeback errors. This change aligns with existing patterns in the code and ensures compliance with the UNSTABLE+COMMIT durability contract.

Last comment 2026-05-20 [PATCH] sunrpc: use kref_get_unless_zero in auth_domain_lookup Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch fixes a bug in the auth_domain_lookup function of the sunrpc module by using kref_get_unless_zero instead of plain kref_get to acquire a reference to an auth_domain entry. This prevents a window where an entry is still linked on the hash list with refcount == 0, which could lead to a dangling reference and object freeing while the caller still holds a pointer to it. The patch applies the same pattern used in the sibling function auth_domain_find to preserve existing semantics.

2 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Chuck Lever ↳ replying to Jeff Layton Inline Review Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer Chuck Lever questioned whether auth_domain_lookup() can encounter a 0-refcount entry due to kref_put_lock()'s behavior, which acquires the spinlock before decrementing the refcount. Reviewer Chuck Lever raised concerns that using kref_get_unless_zero() in auth_domain_lookup() might silently mask a refcount imbalance or use-after-free issue, and also noted that skipping the zero-refcount entry could lead to inserting a duplicate auth_domain into the hash list.
Show original comment 
[Severity: High]
Is this description of kref_put_lock() accurate?

Looking at kref_put_lock(), it uses refcount_dec_and_lock() which acquires
the spinlock before the 1->0 transition is completed. Since
auth_domain_lookup() holds the same auth_domain_lock, is it actually possible
for it to encounter a 0-refcount entry under normal conditions?

---

[Severity: High]
If a 0-refcount entry is encountered here, wouldn't it indicate a severe
underlying refcount imbalance or use-after-free rather than a normal race?

By using kref_get_unless_zero() and continuing the search, might this silently
mask the root cause of the WARN instead of resolving it?

Furthermore, if the loop skips the 0-refcount entry and falls through to the
end of the function, won't it insert a duplicate auth_domain with the same
name into the hash list?

Last comment 2026-05-23 [PATCH v3 00/10] fuse: add io-uring buffer pools and zero-copy 10 patches
Show 10 individual patches
  • [01/10] fuse: separate next request fetching from sending logic
  • [02/10] fuse: refactor io-uring header copying to ring
  • [03/10] fuse: refactor io-uring header copying from ring
  • [04/10] fuse: use enum types for header copying
  • [05/10] fuse: refactor setting up copy state for payload copying
  • [06/10] fuse: use named constants for io-uring iovec indices
  • [07/10] fuse: add io-uring buffer pools (implemented as buffer ring)
  • [08/10] fuse: support registered buffers as buffer pools in io-uring
  • [09/10] fuse: add zero-copy over io-uring
  • [10/10] docs: fuse: add io-uring buffer pool and zero-copy documentation
Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch series adds buffer pools and zero-copy functionality to the fuse io-uring implementation, allowing servers to pass in a managed buffer pool that reduces memory usage requirements and enables future optimizations. It also allows for direct access to client pages or page cache folios without copying data through an intermediary buffer, requiring CAP_SYS_ADMIN privileges. The changes are based on registered buffers and zero-copy, which can provide significant throughput improvements depending on the server's per-request latency and backing I/O characteristics.

14 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Joanne Koong (author) Positive LLM
The author is addressing a concern about duplicated logic in the code, specifically in the fuse_uring_send_next_to_ring() function. They simplified the logic by removing this function and instead calling fuse_uring_prepare_send() directly from fuse_uring_get_next_fuse_req(). The change reduces unnecessary parameter passing and makes the control flow clearer.
Show original comment 
Simplify the logic for fetching + sending off the next request.

This gets rid of fuse_uring_send_next_to_ring() which contained
duplicated logic from fuse_uring_send(). This decouples request fetching
from the send operation, which makes the control flow clearer and
reduces unnecessary parameter passing.

+static int ring_header_type_offset(enum fuse_uring_header_type type)
 {
+	switch (type) {
+	case FUSE_URING_HEADER_IN_OUT:
+		return 0;
+	case FUSE_URING_HEADER_OP:
+		return offsetof(struct fuse_uring_req_header, op_in);

2.52.0
View on lore ↗
Signals: acknowledged a fix is needed, prepared for future changes
Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
The author addressed a concern about the tight coupling between ents and buffers in fuse io-uring by explaining that they have decoupled them, allowing servers to pass in a buffer pool that the kernel will use for servicing ents/requests. The server must set the FUSE_URING_BUFPOOL flag during registration and provide the payload buffer pool through the iovec payload in the first sqe. The author described the internal buffer ring data structure used for managing the buffer pool, including how buffers are selected and recycled.
Show original comment 
Right now, ents and buffers are tightly coupled in fuse io-uring where
each entry has its own dedicated payload buffer, requiring N buffers for
N entries where each buffer must be large enough to accomodate the
maximum payload size. This is suboptimal as most request types (lookup,
open, release, getattr, etc) require vastly less bytes than the maximum
payload size and some requests (unlink, rmdir, fsync, flush, etc) do not
require payload buffers at all.

Instead of requiring a 1:1 coupling between ents and payload buffers,
allow the server to pass in a buffer pool (a contiguous allocation of
buffers) that the kernel will use as it wishes for servicing
ents/requests. Buffers are now pooled and selected on demand. Entries
only "reserve" a buffer while actively processing a request that
requires a payload buffer. This decoupling reduces the memory usage
requirements needed to use fuse-io-uring. It allows for future
optimizations such as incremental buffer consumption which will allow
non-overlapping regions of a single buffer to be used simultaneously
across multiple ents/requests, and the possibility of multiple buffer
sizes to be supported per ring in the future.

To use this, the server must set the FUSE_URING_BUFPOOL flag during
registration and provide the payload buffer pool through the iovec
payload in the first sqe. The server must set init.buf_size and
init.nr_bufs in the struct fuse_uring_cmd_req it passes to the kernel to
describe the buffer pool configuration. Buffer pool usage is set on a
per-ring basis. All subsequent registration SQEs for the same ring must
pass in consistent flags.

Internally, a buffer ring data structure is used for managing the buffer
pool. The kernel manages buffer selection and recycling through this
ring structure. A payload buffer is selected from the ring on demand if
the request requires a payload buffer and recycled after the request
completes if used.

The contiguous buffer pool passed in is partitioned into individual
buffers according to the buf_size passed in at registration time.

  PAYLOAD BUFFER POOL (contiguous, provided via iov[1] in first sqe):
    |<-------------- payload_size ------------>|
    +--------- --+-----------+-----------+-----+
    |  buf [0]   |  buf [1]  |  buf [2]  | ... |
    |  buf_size  |  buf_size |  buf_size | ... |
    +--------- --+-----------+-----------+-----+

The buffer ring logic is as follows:
select:  buf = bufs[head % nbufs]; head++
recycle: bufs[tail % nbufs] = buf; tail++
empty:   tail == head (no buffers available)
full:    tail - head >= nbufs

Buffer ring request flow
------------------------
|  Kernel                                  |  FUSE daemon
|                                          |
|  [client request arrives]                |
|  >fuse_uring_send()                      |
|    [select payload buf from pool]        |
|    >fuse_uring_select_buffer()           |
|    [copy headers to ent]                 |
|    >copy_header_to_ring()                |
|    [copy payload to selected buf]        |
|    >fuse_uring_copy_to_ring()            |
|    [set buf_id in ent_in_out header]     |
|    >io_uring_cmd_done()                  |
|                                          |  [CQE received]
|                                          |  [read headers]
|                                          |  [read payload from buf_id]
|                                          |  [process request]
|                                          |  [write reply to header]
|                                          |  [write reply payload to
|                                          |    buf]
|                                          |  >io_uring_submit()
|                                          |   COMMIT_AND_FETCH
|  >fuse_uring_commit_fetch()              |
|    >fuse_uring_commit()                  |
|     [copy reply from ring]               |
|     >fuse_uring_recycle_buffer()         |
|    >fuse_uring_get_next_fuse_req()       |

Reviewed-by: Jeff Layton <jlayton@kernel.org>
Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>

+static int fuse_uring_get_iovec_from_sqe(const struct io_uring_sqe *sqe,
+					 struct iovec iov[FUSE_URING_IOV_SEGS])
+{
+	struct iovec __user *uiov = u64_to_user_ptr(READ_ONCE(sqe->addr));
+	struct iov_iter iter;
+	ssize_t ret;
+
+	if (sqe->len != FUSE_URING_IOV_SEGS)
+		return -EINVAL;
+
+	/*
+	 * Direction for buffer access will actually be READ and WRITE,
+	 * using write for the import should include READ access as well.
+	 */
+	ret = import_iovec(WRITE, uiov, FUSE_URING_IOV_SEGS,
+			   FUSE_URING_IOV_SEGS, &iov, &iter);
+	if (ret < 0)
+		return ret;
+
+	return 0;
+}

+static int fuse_uring_bufpool_setup(struct io_uring_cmd *cmd,
+				    struct fuse_ring_queue *queue)
+{
+	const struct fuse_uring_cmd_req *cmd_req =
+		io_uring_sqe128_cmd(cmd->sqe, struct fuse_uring_cmd_req);
+	unsigned int buf_size = READ_ONCE(cmd_req->init.buf_size);
+	unsigned int nr_bufs = READ_ONCE(cmd_req->init.nr_bufs);
+	struct iovec iov[FUSE_URING_IOV_SEGS];
+	uintptr_t payload_addr;
+	size_t payload_size, ring_size;
+	struct fuse_bufpool *pool;
+	unsigned int i;
+	int err;
+
+	if (!buf_size || !nr_bufs)
+		return -EINVAL;
+
+	err = fuse_uring_get_iovec_from_sqe(cmd->sqe, iov);
+	if (err)
+		return err;
+
+	payload_addr = (uintptr_t)iov[FUSE_URING_IOV_PAYLOAD].iov_base;
+	payload_size = iov[FUSE_URING_IOV_PAYLOAD].iov_len;
+
+	if (payload_size < (uint64_t)buf_size * nr_bufs)
+		return -EINVAL;
+
+	/* create the pool, which is managed as a ring buffer */
+	ring_size = struct_size(pool, bufs, nr_bufs);
+	pool = kzalloc(ring_size, GFP_KERNEL_ACCOUNT);
+	if (!pool)
+		return -ENOMEM;
+
+	/* populate the ring buffer */
+	for (i = 0; i < nr_bufs; i++, payload_addr += buf_size) {
+		struct fuse_bufpool_buf *buf = &pool->bufs[i];
+
+		buf->addr = payload_addr;
+		buf->len = buf_size;
+		buf->id = i;
+	}
+
+	pool->nbufs = nr_bufs;
+	pool->tail = nr_bufs;
+
+	queue->bufpool = pool;
+
+	return 0;
+}
+
+/*
+ * If the queue is already registered, check that the queue was initialized with
+ * the same init flags set for this FUSE_IO_URING_CMD_REGISTER cmd. all
+ * FUSE_IO_URING_CMD_REGISTER cmds should have the same init fields set on a
+ * per-queue basis.
+ */
+static bool queue_init_flags_consistent(struct fuse_ring_queue *queue,
+					u64 init_flags)
+{
+	bool bufpool = init_flags & FUSE_URING_BUFPOOL;
+
+	return bufpool_enabled(queue) == bufpool;
+}

+static bool fuse_uring_req_has_payload(struct fuse_req *req)
+{
+	struct fuse_args *args = req->args;

+static int fuse_uring_select_buffer(struct fuse_ring_ent *ent)
+{
+	struct fuse_ring_queue *queue = ent->queue;
+	struct fuse_bufpool *pool = queue->bufpool;
+	struct fuse_bufpool_buf *buf;
+	unsigned int tail = pool->tail, head = pool->head;
+
+	lockdep_assert_held(&queue->lock);
+
+	if (tail == head)
+		return -ENOBUFS;
+
+	buf = &pool->bufs[head % pool->nbufs];
+	pool->head++;
+
+	ent->payload_buf = *buf;
+
+	return 0;
+}
+
+static void fuse_uring_recycle_buffer(struct fuse_ring_ent *ent)
+{
+	struct fuse_bufpool_buf *ent_payload = &ent->payload_buf;
+	struct fuse_ring_queue *queue = ent->queue;
+	struct fuse_bufpool_buf *buf;
+	struct fuse_bufpool *pool;
+
+	lockdep_assert_held(&queue->lock);
+
+	if (!bufpool_enabled(queue) || !ent_payload->addr)
+		return;
+
+	pool = queue->bufpool;
+
+	/* pool should never be full */
+	WARN_ON_ONCE(pool->tail - pool->head >= pool->nbufs);
+
+	buf = &pool->bufs[(pool->tail) % pool->nbufs];
+	*buf = *ent_payload;
+
+	pool->tail++;
+
+	memset(ent_payload, 0, sizeof(*ent_payload));
+}
+
+static int fuse_uring_next_req_update_buffer(struct fuse_ring_ent *ent,
+					     struct fuse_req *req)
+{
+	bool buffer_selected;
+	bool has_payload;
+
+	if (!bufpool_enabled(ent->queue))
+		return 0;
+
+	buffer_selected = !!ent->payload_buf.addr;
+	has_payload = fuse_uring_req_has_payload(req);
+
+	if (has_payload && !buffer_selected)
+		return fuse_uring_select_buffer(ent);
+
+	if (!has_payload && buffer_selected)
+		fuse_uring_recycle_buffer(ent);
+
+	return 0;
+}
+
+static int fuse_uring_prep_buffer(struct fuse_ring_ent *ent,
+				  struct fuse_req *req)
+{
+	if (!bufpool_enabled(ent->queue))
+		return 0;
+
+	/* no payload to copy, can skip selecting a buffer */
+	if (!fuse_uring_req_has_payload(req))
+		return 0;
+
+	return fuse_uring_select_buffer(ent);
+}

2.52.0
View on lore ↗
Signals: clarification, explanation
Joanne Koong (author) Positive LLM
The author addressed a concern about the overhead of pinning/unpinning user pages and translating virtual addresses per i/o request, explaining that registered buffers eliminate this overhead by pinning pages upfront. The author provided details on how to use registered buffers, including setting specific flags in the registration sqe and following standard protocol for using registered buffers.
Show original comment 
Allow servers to use an io-uring registered buffer as the buffer pool.
When the server registers buffers with io-uring, the pages backing the
buffers are pinned upfront. This eliminates the overhead of
pinning/unpinning user pages and translating virtual addresses per i/o
request. This also allows servers to use the same registered buffers for
subsequent backing store I/O (eg read_fixed/write_fixed), keeping data
in the same pinned pages without additional pinning or mapping overhead
required.

Registered buffers require the buffer pool (FUSE_URING_BUFPOOL) to be
enabled. To use registered buffers, the server needs to register the
payload buffers through io-uring and during registration, set the
FUSE_URING_REGISTERED_BUFFERS init flag (alongside the
FUSE_URING_BUFPOOL flag) in the registration sqe. For all sqes the
server passes in (including the registration ones), it needs to follow
standard protocol for using registered buffers (eg set
sqe->uring_cmd_flags to include IORING_URING_CMD_FIXED, and pass in the
index where the registered buffers reside to sqe->buf_index).

In benchmarks using passthrough_hp on a high-performance NVMe-backed
system, using registered buffers showed around a 10% throughput
improvement for direct randreads (~2150 MiB/s to ~2400 MiB/s), a 4%
improvement for direct sequential reads (~2510 MiB/s to ~2620 MiB/s),
a 8% improvement for buffered randreads (~2100 MiB/s to ~2280 MiB/s),
and a 6% improvement for buffered sequential reads (~2500 MiB/s to
~2670 MiB/s).

Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>

2.52.0
View on lore ↗
Signals: acknowledged a fix is needed, provided explanation
Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
The author addressed a concern about the zero-copy implementation, specifically the request flow and registration/unregistration path for page-backed and non-page-backed arguments. The author provided detailed explanations of the zero-copy read and write paths, including the use of io_buffer_register_bvec() and fuse_uring_set_up_zero_copy(). They confirmed that the server can directly access client pages or page cache folios without copying data through an intermediary buffer, but noted that this requires CAP_SYS_ADMIN privileges. The author also acknowledged that some requests may have both page-backed and non-page-backed arguments, which are handled differently in the zero-copy implementation.
Show original comment 
Implement zero-copy for fuse io-uring, eliminating memory copies between
userspace, the kernel, and the fuse server for read/write operations.
The server can directly access client pages or page cache folios without
copying data through an intermediary buffer. When a fuse request arrives,
the kernel registers the relevant pages into a sparse slot in the
server's io_uring registered buffer table. The server can then operate
on these pages directly using io-uring fixed buffer operations (eg
read_fixed/write_fixed) and the kernel unregisters these pages when the
request completes. Non-page-backed args (eg op out headers) will go
through the payload buffer as normal.

This requires CAP_SYS_ADMIN and FUSE_URING_REGISTERED_BUFFERS (which
requires using bufpools). Gating on registered buffers keeps the
configuration space small and avoids partially-optimized modes that are
unlikely to be useful in practice. This is gated behind CAP_SYS_ADMIN
because zero-copy allows the server direct access to the client's
underlying pages, rather than operating on an intermediary buffer that
the contents of the client's pages were copied into or on page cache
folios.

The request flow for the zero-copy write path (client writes data,
server reads it) is as follows:
=======================================================================
|  Kernel                                   |  FUSE server
|                                           |
|  "write(fd, buf, 1MB)"                    |
|                                           |
|  >sys_write()                             |
|    >fuse_file_write_iter()                |
|      >fuse_send_one()                     |
|        [req->args->in_pages = true]       |
|        [folios hold client write data]    |
|                                           |
|  >fuse_uring_copy_to_ring()               |
|    >copy_header_to_ring(IN_OUT)           |
|      [memcpy fuse_in_header]              |
|    >copy_header_to_ring(OP)               |
|      [memcpy write_in header]             |
|                                           |
|    >fuse_uring_args_to_ring()             |
|      >setup_fuse_copy_state()             |
|        [skip_folio_copy = true]           |
|                                           |
|      >fuse_uring_set_up_zero_copy()       |
|        [folio_get for each client folio]  |
|        [build bio_vec array from folios]  |
|        >io_buffer_register_bvec()         |
|          [register pages at
                 ent->zero_copy_index]      |
|        [ent->zero_copied = true]          |
|                                           |
|      >fuse_copy_args()                    |
|        [skip_folio_copy => return 0       |
|         for page arg, skip data copy]     |
|                                           |
|    >copy_header_to_ring(RING_ENT)         |
|      [memcpy ent_in_out]                  |
|    >io_uring_cmd_done()                   |
|                                           |
|                                           | [CQE received]
|                                           |
|                                           | [issue io_uring READ at
|                                           |  ent->zero_copy_index]
|                                           | [reads directly from
|                                           |client's pages (ZERO_COPY)]
|                                           |
|                                           | [write data to backing
|                                           | store]
|                                           |  [submit COMMIT AND FETCH]
|                                           |
|  >fuse_uring_commit_fetch()               |
|    >fuse_uring_commit()                   |
|      >fuse_uring_copy_from_ring()         |
|    >fuse_uring_req_end()                  |
|      >io_buffer_unregister(ent->zero_copy_index) |
|        [unregister sparse buffer]         |
|      >fuse_zero_copy_release()            |
|        [folio_put for each folio]         |
|      [ent->zero_copied = false]           |
|      >fuse_request_end()                  |
|        [wake up client]                   |

The zero-copy read path is analogous.

Some requests may have both page-backed args and non-page-backed args.
For these requests, the page-backed args are zero-copied while the
non-page-backed args are copied to the buffer selected from the buffer
ring:
    zero-copy: pages registered via io_buffer_register_bvec()
    non-page-backed: copied to payload buffer via fuse_copy_args()

For a request whose payload is zero-copied, the
registration/unregistration path looks like:

    register:  fuse_uring_set_up_zero_copy()
                 folio_get() for each folio
                 io_buffer_register_bvec(ent->zero_copy_index)

    unregister: fuse_uring_req_end()
                  io_buffer_unregister(ent->zero_copy_index)
                  -> fuse_zero_copy_release() callback
                     folio_put() for each folio

The throughput improvement from zero-copy depends on how much of the
per-request latency is spent on data copying vs backing I/O. When
backing I/O dominates, the saved memcpy is a negligible fraction of
overall latency. Please also note that for the server to read/write
into the zero-copied pages, the read/write must go through io-uring
as an IORING_OP_READ_FIXED / IORING_OP_WRITE_FIXED operation. If the
server's backing I/O is instantaneous (eg served from cache), the
overhead of the additional io_uring operation may negate the savings
from eliminating the memcpy.

In benchmarks using passthrough_hp on a high-performance NVMe-backed
system, zero-copy showed around a 35% throughput improvement for direct
randreads (~2150 MiB/s to ~2900 MiB/s), a 15% improvement for direct
sequential reads (~2510 MiB/s to ~2900 MiB/s), a 15% improvement for
buffered randreads (~2100 MiB/s to ~2470 MiB/s), and a 10% improvement
for buffered sequential reads (~2500 MiB/s to ~2750 MiB/s).

The benchmarks were run using:
  fio --name=test_run --ioengine=sync --rw=rand{read,write} --bs=1M
  --size=1G --numjobs=2 --ramp_time=30 --group_reporting=1

Reviewed-by: Jeff Layton <jlayton@kernel.org>
Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>

+static void fuse_zero_copy_release(void *priv)
+{
+	struct fuse_zero_copy_bvs *zc_bvs = priv;
+	unsigned int i;
+
+	for (i = 0; i < zc_bvs->nr_bvs; i++)
+		folio_put(page_folio(zc_bvs->bvs[i].bv_page));
+
+	kfree(zc_bvs);
+}
+
+static int fuse_uring_set_up_zero_copy(struct fuse_ring_ent *ent,
+				       struct fuse_req *req,
+				       unsigned int issue_flags)
+{
+	struct fuse_args_pages *ap;
+	int err, i, ddir = 0;
+	struct fuse_zero_copy_bvs *zc_bvs;
+	struct bio_vec *bvs;
+
+	/* out_pages indicates a read, in_pages indicates a write */
+	if (req->args->out_pages)
+		ddir |= IO_BUF_DEST;
+	if (req->args->in_pages)
+		ddir |= IO_BUF_SOURCE;
+
+	WARN_ON_ONCE(!ddir);
+
+	ap = container_of(req->args, typeof(*ap), args);
+
+	zc_bvs = kmalloc(struct_size(zc_bvs, bvs, ap->num_folios),
+			 GFP_KERNEL_ACCOUNT);
+	if (!zc_bvs)
+		return -ENOMEM;
+
+	zc_bvs->nr_bvs = ap->num_folios;
+	bvs = zc_bvs->bvs;
+	for (i = 0; i < ap->num_folios; i++) {
+		bvs[i].bv_page = folio_page(ap->folios[i], 0);
+		bvs[i].bv_offset = ap->descs[i].offset;
+		bvs[i].bv_len = ap->descs[i].length;
+		folio_get(ap->folios[i]);
+	}
+
+	err = io_buffer_register_bvec(ent->cmd, bvs, ap->num_folios,
+				      fuse_zero_copy_release, zc_bvs,
+				      ddir, ent->zero_copy_index,
+				      issue_flags);
+	if (err) {
+		fuse_zero_copy_release(zc_bvs);
+		return err;
+	}
+
+	ent->zero_copied = true;
+
+	return 0;
+}

  */

Joanne Koong (author) ↳ replying to Bernd Schubert Needs Work LLM
Author acknowledged that header pinning was removed from the patchset and is being addressed separately, confirming it's not a concern for this specific series. Author agrees that payload buffers should be decoupled from ring entries to reduce memory usage, but does not provide a clear plan for addressing this issue. The author addressed a concern about header pinning by explaining that the headers are stored in a single contiguous region, thus avoiding the need for separate pages per entry. The author is addressing a concern about zero-copy functionality in the patch series, specifically that many servers may not be able to use it due to CAP_SYS_ADMIN requirements. The author acknowledges this limitation and suggests minimizing memory consumption for the non-zero-copy path through buffer pools.
Show original comment 
Hi Bernd,

Header pinning was dropped from this patchset. I have a separate
branch that has header pinning alongside the changes for avoiding the
fuse io_uring_cmd_complete_in_task() deferral. I moved the header
pinning changes out of this patchset as it doesn't tie in with getting
perf improvements from using registered buffers, unlike payload buffer
pinning.

---

I think payload buffers must be decoupled from ring entries if we want
to reduce memory usage in the non-zero-copy path.

---

For the header pinning changes in my branch, the headers are one
contiguous region (not per-entry), which circumvents having to
allocate one page per entry.

---

For zero-copy, entries still may have payloads (though the buffers
will definitely not need to be as big as the max payload size!),
either for the non-zero-copyable args or if the request's args aren't
page-backed. Unfortunately I think many servers may not be able to use
zero-copy due to the CAP_SYS_ADMIN requirements, so I think it'd be
ideal to minimize the memory consumption needed for the non-zero-copy
path, through the buffer pool for the payload buffers.

I hope I'm interpreting your question correctly - if not, please let me know!

Thanks,
Joanne

Signals: requested changes
Joanne Koong (author) ↳ replying to Bernd Schubert Neutral LLM
The author addressed concerns about the buffer pool implementation, explaining that entries can be used for servicing requests even if there are fewer buffers than entries. They also highlighted the benefits of decoupling ents and buffers, including supporting multiple buffer sizes per ring and eliminating the need for payload buffers in certain requests.
Show original comment 
Entries may be used for servicing requests even if there are less
buffers than the number of entries. Most requests don't use the full
payload buffer size, so for example with incremental buffer
consumption, this would allow multiple entries to use non-overlapping
regions of the same buffer concurrently. As well, if we want to
support multiple buffer sizes per ring, there shouldn't be a 1:1
mapping between ents and buffers. There's also some requests that
don't need to use payload buffers at all (eg flush, fsync, rmdir,
etc).  As well for registered buffers / buffer pinning, it is more
optimal for the buffer pool to be allocated contiguously and pinned
contiguously rather than passed in one by one as a 1:1 entry:buffer
mapping.

Thanks,
Joanne

Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch series extends the FUSE (Filesystem in Userspace) passthrough feature to support inode operations, including getattr, setattr, and readdir. The existing passthrough mode is modified to introduce a stricter mode called FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO, which requires one-to-one inode number mapping for attaching a backing file to a fuse inode. This allows for more efficient handling of inode operations and improves test results in certain scenarios.

11 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
The author addressed a concern about the one-to-one inode number mapping in FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO mode, explaining that it requires 64-bit inode support and will limit the possibility of mapping multiple fuse inodes to the same backing file unless they are hardlinks. The author did not indicate any plans for a fix or revision.
Show original comment 
From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

This is a more strict variant of FUSE_PASSTHROUGH mode, in which the
backing file inode number must match the fuse inode number.

This mode will allow the kernel to instantiate fuse inodes by
passthrough lookup and passthrough readdirplus and notify about those
inodes to the server, using the backing file inode number as a unique
identifier for fuse inodes across kernel and server.

This mode limits the possibility to map multiple fuse inodes to the same
backing file, unless they are all hardlinks.

This mode is only supported on 64bit arch, where ino_t is u64.

Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

2.52.0

---

From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

So far, fuse passthrough was implemented for read/write/splice/mmap
operations for regular files opened with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.

A backing file is attached to a fuse inode, but only for as long as
there are FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH files opened on this inode.

We would like to attach a backing file to fuse inode also without an
open file to allow passthrough of some inode operations.

Add field ops_mask to the input argument of FUSE_DEV_IOC_BACKING_OPEN
ioctl to declare the operations that would passthrough to the backing
file once it has been attached to the fuse inode on lookup.

Setting the FUSE_READ/FUSE_WRITE operations in the ops_mask is not
required because those operations are implied by FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.

When setting operations other than FUSE_READ/FUSE_WRITE in ops_mask,
non-regular backing files are allowed, so we need to verify when
attaching a backing file to a fuse inode, that their file types match.

For simplification of inode attribute caching, for now, require a
filesystem with FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO (one-to-one mapping from fuse inode
to backing inode) for setting up passthrough of any inode operations.
We may consider relaxing this requirement for some inode operations
in the future.

Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

+	 * creation/lookup time.
+	 */
+	err = -EOPNOTSUPP;
+	if (!fuse_inode_backing(fi) &&
+	    (fb->ops_mask & FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INODE_OPS))
+		goto fail;
+
 	/* First passthrough file open denies caching inode io mode */
 	err = fuse_file_uncached_io_open(inode, ff, fb);
 	if (!err)
 		return 0;
 
+fail:
 	fuse_passthrough_release(ff, fb);
 	fuse_backing_put(fb);

2.52.0

---

From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

In preparation for readdir passthrough, allow the inode iomode state
to be applicable to directory inodes and prepare the helper
fuse_sync_release() for directories.

Directory inodes will support cached mode, "direct" uncached readdir
mode and readdir passthrough mode, but will not need to wait for
parallel dio like regular files.

Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

2.52.0
View on lore ↗
Signals: clarification, explanation
Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
The author addressed a concern about the interaction between FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH and FOPEN_CACHE_DIR flags in directory opens, explaining that both flags are required for readdir passthrough and that a directory opened without both flags is marked as FOPEN_DIRECT_IO. The author noted that this behavior is similar to regular files.
Show original comment 
From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

Requires both requesting the passthrough inode op READDIR when setting
up the backing file and opening the dir with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.

The dir opened with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH must not request cached readdir
with FOPEN_CACHE_DIR flag.

Like regular files, a directory inode cannot be opened at the same time
for cached readdir and readdir passthrough.

A directory opened without both FOPEN_CACHE_DIR and FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH
is marked as FOPEN_DIRECT_IO and does not affect io mode.

Note that opt-in for passthrough of READDIR operation means that there
is no READDIRPLUS call to server.

For the ls -l use case, the cost of FUSE_LOOKUP to server will be
paid for every entry, so passthrough of READDIR is not always a
performance win.

Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

2.52.0

---

From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

Currently backing file is attached to fuse inode on the first
passthrough open of the inode and detached on last passthrough close.

In preparation for attaching a backing file to inode with no open file,
allow attaching a single long lived reference on fuse inode backing file
that will be used for passthrough of inode operations and detached on
fuse inode evict.

From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

Call vfs_getattr() on backing inode to respond to a user statx(2)
request and update the fuse inode attributes with the response.

For now, we assume that calling vfs_getattr() on backing inode is cheap,
so we never use cached attributed and always update fuse inode
attributes from backing attributes in fuse_permission() and
fuse_update_attributes().

+void fuse_kstat_to_attr(struct fuse_conn *fc, const struct kstat *stat,
+			struct fuse_attr *attr)
+{
+	memset(attr, 0, sizeof(*attr));
+
+	attr->ino = stat->ino;
+	attr->size = stat->size;
+	attr->blocks = stat->blocks;
+	attr->atime = stat->atime.tv_sec;
+	attr->mtime = stat->mtime.tv_sec;
+	attr->ctime = stat->ctime.tv_sec;
+	attr->atimensec = stat->atime.tv_nsec;
+	attr->mtimensec = stat->mtime.tv_nsec;
+	attr->ctimensec = stat->ctime.tv_nsec;
+	attr->mode = stat->mode;
+	attr->nlink = stat->nlink;
+	attr->uid = from_kuid(fc->user_ns, stat->uid);
+	attr->gid = from_kgid(fc->user_ns, stat->gid);
+	attr->rdev = new_encode_dev(MKDEV(MAJOR(stat->rdev), MINOR(stat->rdev)));
+	attr->blksize = stat->blksize;
+}

diff --git a/fs/fuse/passthrough.c b/fs/fuse/passthrough.c

+/*
+ * Inode passthrough operations for backing file attached on lookup.
+ */
+int fuse_passthrough_getattr(struct inode *inode, struct kstat *stat,
+			     u32 request_mask, unsigned int flags)
+{
+	struct fuse_conn *fc = get_fuse_conn(inode);
+	struct fuse_inode *fi = get_fuse_inode(inode);
+	struct fuse_backing *fb = fuse_inode_backing(fi);
+	u64 attr_version = fuse_get_attr_version(fc);
+	const struct path *fb_path = &fb->file->f_path;
+	const struct cred *old_cred;
+	struct kstat backing_stat;
+	struct fuse_attr attr;
+	int err;
+
+	if (!stat)
+		stat = &backing_stat;
+
+	old_cred = override_creds(fb->cred);
+	err = vfs_getattr(fb_path, stat, request_mask, flags);
+	revert_creds(old_cred);
+	if (err)
+		return err;
+
+	/* Always override st_dev and st_ino with FUSE dev and ino */
+	stat->dev = inode->i_sb->s_dev;
+	stat->ino = inode->i_ino;
+
+	/* Fill fuse inode attrs from backing inode stat */
+	fuse_kstat_to_attr(fc, stat, &attr);
+	fuse_change_attributes(inode, &attr, NULL, 0, attr_version);
+
+	return 0;
+}

2.52.0

---

From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

Add a helper for requesting to associate a backing inode for inode
passthrough operations.

This helper is expected to be used to setup backing inode on lookup
response.

The minimal requirement for the backing inode is to support the
GETATTR passthrough op.

Unlike setting of passthrough from open, this mapping is created for
the entire lifetime of the inode and cannot be changed later.

Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>

+/*
+ * Get fuse backing object by backing id.
+ *
+ * Returns an fb object with elevated refcount to be stored in fuse inode.
+ */
+struct fuse_backing *fuse_backing_id_get(struct fuse_conn *fc, int backing_id)
+{
+	struct fuse_backing *fb;
+
+	if (backing_id <= 0)
+		return ERR_PTR(-EINVAL);
+
+	rcu_read_lock();
+	fb = idr_find(&fc->backing_files_map, backing_id);
+	fb = fuse_backing_get(fb);
+	rcu_read_unlock();
+
+	return fb;
+}

+/* Setup passthrough for inode operations without an open file */
+int fuse_inode_set_passthrough(struct inode *inode, int backing_id)
+{
+	struct fuse_conn *fc = get_fuse_conn(inode);
+	struct fuse_inode *fi = get_fuse_inode(inode);
+	struct fuse_backing *current_fb, *fb;
+	int err;
+
+	if (!IS_ENABLED(CONFIG_FUSE_PASSTHROUGH) || !fc->passthrough_ino)
+		return 0;
+
+	fb = fuse_backing_id_get(fc, backing_id);
+	if (IS_ERR_OR_NULL(fb)) {
+		err = fb ? PTR_ERR(fb) : -ENOENT;
+		fb = NULL;
+		goto fail;
+	}
+
+	current_fb = fuse_inode_backing(fi);
+	if (current_fb) {
+		/* Different backing file on same inode is not allowed */
+		err = current_fb == fb ? 0 : -EBUSY;
+		fuse_backing_put(fb);
+		return err;
+	}
+
+	/* Backing inode requires at least GETATTR op passthrough */
+	err = -EOPNOTSUPP;
+	if (!(fb->ops_mask & FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP_GETATTR))
+		goto fail;
+
+	err = fuse_inode_uncached_io_start(inode, NULL, fb);
+	if (err)
+		goto fail;
+
+	return 0;
+fail:
+	fuse_backing_put(fb);
+	pr_debug("failed to setup backing inode (ino=%lu, backing_id=%d, err=%i).\n",
+		 inode->i_ino, backing_id, err);
+	return err;
+}

  * Open flags that are allowed in combination with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.
  * A combination of FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH and FOPEN_DIRECT_IO means that read/write

2.52.0
View on lore ↗
Signals: clarification, explanation
Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
The author addressed a concern about maintaining backwards compatibility for servers that pre-date the ops_mask field. They agreed to default the ops_mask to FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_RW_OPS in such cases, while requiring an explicit ops_mask for FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO servers.
Show original comment 
Servers that pre-date the ops_mask field will pass a zero ops_mask in
FUSE_DEV_IOC_BACKING_OPEN. Default this to FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_RW_OPS to
maintain backwards compatibility.

For FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO servers, an ops_mask must be set.
FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO is a new feature with no backwards compatibliity
requirements.

Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>

 		goto out;
 
-	/* For now passthrough inode operations requires FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO */
-	if (!fc->passthrough_ino && map->ops_mask & FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INODE_OPS)
-		goto out;
+	if (!fc->passthrough_ino) {
+		/*
+		 * For now passthrough inode operations requires
+		 * FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO
+		 */
+		if (map->ops_mask & FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INODE_OPS)
+			goto out;
+		/*
+		 * To maintain backwards compatibility with servers that
+		 * pre-date the ops_mask field, a zero ops_mask defaults
+		 * to passing through both reads and writes
+		 */
+		if (!map->ops_mask)
+			map->ops_mask |= FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_RW_OPS;
+	} else if (!map->ops_mask) {
+		return -EINVAL;
+	}
 
 	file = fget_raw(map->fd);
 	res = -EBADF;
-- 
2.52.0

---

Servers can now pass through only reads or writes instead of being
required to pass through both. When the read or write operation is not
passed through, fall back to direct io for handling it. This avoids
cache coherency issues from mixing the backing file's page cache with
the fuse inode's page cache.

Reject mmap when passthrough is partial or not set for read/writes since
mmap requires both read and write access to the backing page cache.

The FOPEN_DIRECT_IO check in the read/write fallback is not strictly
needed as the caller already handles it, but including it here makes
the fallback logic self-contained.

Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
---

On Fri, May 15, 2026 at 5:53 PM Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Add passthrough setattr which sets attributes directly on the backing
> inode through backing_inode_setattr() instead of sending FUSE_SETATTR to
> the server.
>
> Passthrough setattr is checked before the
> handle_killpriv/handle_killpriv_v2 suid/sgid stripping because the
> stripping is handled natively by notify_change() on the backing inode.
>
> Signed-off-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
> ---
>  fs/fuse/dir.c             |  3 +++
>  fs/fuse/fuse_i.h          |  3 ++-
>  fs/fuse/passthrough.c     | 28 ++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
>  include/uapi/linux/fuse.h |  1 +
>  4 files changed, 34 insertions(+), 1 deletion(-)
>
> diff --git a/fs/fuse/dir.c b/fs/fuse/dir.c
> index 4c7e3e1604af..b67b3b334e69 100644
> --- a/fs/fuse/dir.c
> +++ b/fs/fuse/dir.c
> @@ -2506,6 +2506,9 @@ static int fuse_setattr(struct mnt_idmap *idmap, struct dentry *entry,
>         if (!fuse_allow_current_process(get_fuse_conn(inode)))
>                 return -EACCES;
>
> +       if (fuse_passthrough_op(inode, FUSE_SETATTR))
> +               return fuse_passthrough_setattr(entry, attr);

In the v1 discussion [1], there was a suggestion about gating
FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO on FUSE_HANDLE_KILLPRIV_V2 to avoid the
non-atomic killpriv path, but I think we were only encountering the
non-atomic killpriv path because I was calling
fuse_passthrough_setattr() in the wrong place. I think we can avoid
this altogether by just having the backing filesystem handle all of
the suid/sgid stripping atomically through its own notify_change()
path, which will let us skip all the fuse killpriv handling logic in
this function.

Thanks,
Joanne

[1] https://lore.kernel.org/fuse-devel/CAOQ4uxipQJt5zskb_THxueGi_MXpFdywFiGpd_nmWeY_sMHwzQ@mail.gmail.com/

> +
>         if (attr->ia_valid & (ATTR_KILL_SUID | ATTR_KILL_SGID)) {
>                 attr->ia_valid &= ~(ATTR_KILL_SUID | ATTR_KILL_SGID |
>                                     ATTR_MODE);

On Fri, May 15, 2026 at 5:53 PM Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com> wrote:

>                          * ia_mode calculation may have used stale i_mode.

>                          */
> -                       ret = fuse_do_getattr(idmap, inode, NULL, file);

> +                                                              STATX_MODE, 0);
> +                       else
> +                               ret = fuse_do_getattr(idmap, inode, NULL, file);

I left this part untouched from v1 but there was a discussion [1]
about whether to enforce that setattr must be passed through if
getattr is passed through [1]. I think there might be some use cases
though where having only getattr passed through and not setattr is
useful (eg server wants fast stat() but needs to intercept attribute
changes for access control or policy enforcement). I'm not sure if you
still feel it's better to keep it simple with enforcing that
getattr+setattr rmust always be passed through together, Amir, but if
so I'm happy to add that in.

Thanks,
Joanne

On Fri, May 15, 2026 at 5:52 PM Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> From: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>
>
> So far, fuse passthrough was implemented for read/write/splice/mmap
> operations for regular files opened with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.
>
> A backing file is attached to a fuse inode, but only for as long as
> there are FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH files opened on this inode.
>
> We would like to attach a backing file to fuse inode also without an
> open file to allow passthrough of some inode operations.
>
> Add field ops_mask to the input argument of FUSE_DEV_IOC_BACKING_OPEN
> ioctl to declare the operations that would passthrough to the backing
> file once it has been attached to the fuse inode on lookup.
>
> Setting the FUSE_READ/FUSE_WRITE operations in the ops_mask is not
> required because those operations are implied by FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH.
>
> When setting operations other than FUSE_READ/FUSE_WRITE in ops_mask,
> non-regular backing files are allowed, so we need to verify when
> attaching a backing file to a fuse inode, that their file types match.
>
> For simplification of inode attribute caching, for now, require a
> filesystem with FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO (one-to-one mapping from fuse inode
> to backing inode) for setting up passthrough of any inode operations.
> We may consider relaxing this requirement for some inode operations
> in the future.
>
> Reviewed-by: Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com>
> Signed-off-by: Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com>
> ---
>  fs/fuse/backing.c         | 13 ++++++++++---
>  fs/fuse/fuse_i.h          | 30 ++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
>  fs/fuse/iomode.c          | 16 ++++++++++++++++
>  include/uapi/linux/fuse.h |  9 ++++++++-
>  4 files changed, 64 insertions(+), 4 deletions(-)
>
> diff --git a/include/uapi/linux/fuse.h b/include/uapi/linux/fuse.h
> index 4be9ccc5b3ff..0f1e1c1ec367 100644
> --- a/include/uapi/linux/fuse.h
> +++ b/include/uapi/linux/fuse.h
> @@ -243,6 +243,7 @@
>
> +#define FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP(op)        (1ULL << ((op) - 1))
> +
> +/* op bits for fuse_backing_map ops_mask */
> +#define FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP_READ       FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP(FUSE_READ)
> +#define FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP_WRITE      FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP(FUSE_WRITE)

Do you think we should couple the passthrough op code to the fuse
opcode so closely, instead of defining the passthrough ops separately,
eg doing something like this?:

#define FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_READ         (1 << 0)
#define FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_WRITE       (1 << 1)

In the (far) future when some more advanced passthrough features get
added (eg full subtree passthrough), it seems like we'd want to add a
passthrough op for that, but that wouldn't map to a fuse op. I think
there are also some fuse ops we might skip defining as passthrough ops
but are implicitly passed through (eg FUSE_STATX which is covered by
FUSE_GETATTR), so it seems more intuitive to define the passthrough
ops as describing capabilities rather than implying that it describes
what specific opcodes get passed through?

Thanks,
Joanne

Joanne Koong (author) Neutral LLM
Author acknowledged that server passing through GETATTR and opening files in caching mode is not currently supported, but proposed two options: either document the reason for requiring FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH or relax the limitation by allowing cached io mode.

On Sat, May 16, 2026 at 1:59 PM Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> On Sat, May 16, 2026 at 8:23 PM Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com> wrote:

> > >
> > > Add section about extended passthrough (FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO) mode.
> > >

> > >  .../filesystems/fuse/fuse-passthrough.rst     | 126 ++++++++++++++++++

> > > @@ -25,6 +25,11 @@ operations.
> > >
> > > +Extended Passthrough (FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO)
> > > +============================================
> > > +
> > > +``FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO`` is a stricter variant of ``FUSE_PASSTHROUGH`` in
> > > +which the backing file inode number must match the fuse inode number, enforcing
> > > +a one-to-one mapping. The kernel offers this flag during ``FUSE_INIT`` if
> > > +``CONFIG_FUSE_PASSTHROUGH`` is enabled and the architecture has 64-bit
> > > +``ino_t``. The daemon accepts by returning it back in the init reply.
> >
> > IIUC, ino_t is now always 64-bit.

When Jeff's changes for u64 inode->i_ino land in the fuse tree, I'll
get rid of this and update the 1st patch accordingly.

> >
> > > +
> > > +IO Mode State Machine
> > > +---------------------
> > > +
> > > +The ``iocachectr`` field in ``struct fuse_inode`` prevents conflicting access
> > > +modes on the same inode (page-cache I/O and passthrough I/O cannot coexist)::
> > > +
> > > +    iocachectr > 0    Cached mode
> > > +    iocachectr == 0   Idle. No files open, no passthrough
> >
> > More accurately, no open files in caching or passthough.
> > files open with FOPEN_DIRECT_IO may exist and they
> > do not deny entering either caching or passthrough iomode.

Good point, I'll update this to be more precise.

> >
> > > +    iocachectr < 0    Uncached/passthrough mode
> > > +
> > > +Each open file in passthrough mode holds one reference (``iocachectr--``).
> > > +The inode-level passthrough setup holds one additional long-lived reference
> > > +if the backing has inode ops (getattr/setattr). This long-lived reference is
> > > +released on inode eviction.
> > > +
> > > +Cached mode and passthrough mode are mutually exclusive. Attempting either
> > > +while the other is active returns ``-ETXTBSY``.
> > > +
> > > +For directories, the same mechanism arbitrates between cached readdir
> > > +(``FOPEN_CACHE_DIR``) and passthrough readdir. A directory opened without
> > > +``FOPEN_CACHE_DIR`` and without ``FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH`` is treated as direct I/O
> > > +and does not affect io mode.
> > > +
> > > +Things to note
> > > +--------------
> > > +
> > > +- ``FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_INO`` requires 64-bit ``ino_t``.
> >
> > Not relevant I think.
> >
> > > +- Readdirplus does not set up inode passthrough. Inodes created via readdirplus
> > > +  use normal FUSE operations until a fresh lookup occurs.
> > > +- An inode's backing association is set once and cannot be changed.
> > > +- Passthrough and cached I/O cannot coexist on the same inode.
> > > +- If any inode operations are passed through, this means all opened files need
> > > +  to set the ``FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH`` flag in the open response, even if reads
> > > +  and writes are not passed through. If reads and writes are not passed
> > > +  through, they will go directly to the daemon.
> >
> > I had not considered this.
> > Setting OP_GETATTR/SETATTR in LOOKUP without any OP_RW bits
> > and then requiring that the server open files with FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH
> > with the backing_id sounds strange -
> > I understand why it was done this way, but for users this could be perplexing.
> >
> > The thing is that if the server is only doing GETATTR passthrough there is not
> > really a reason to deny open file in caching mode (I think?).
> >
> > The limitation that requires FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH is encoded in
> > fuse_file_cached_io_open()
> >     fuse_is_io_cache_wait()
> >         !fuse_inode_backing()
> >
> > We have two options.
> >
> > Either we decide that server passing through GETATTR and opening
> > files in caching mode is not interesting to support (for now) and then just
> > maybe we need to better document the reason that server needs to
> > use FOPEN_PASSTHROUGH despite not doing io passthrough.
> >
> > Or we relax the limitation w.r.t cached io mode, something like this
> > (completely untested most likely broken based or earlier review
> > suggestion regarding fuse_passthrough_op):
> >
> > Thanks,
> > Amir.
> >
> > diff --git a/fs/fuse/iomode.c b/fs/fuse/iomode.c
> > index c5f3e2201c6ab..7c33e7a974f6c 100644
> > --- a/fs/fuse/iomode.c
> > +++ b/fs/fuse/iomode.c
> > @@ -20,7 +20,8 @@ static inline bool fuse_is_io_cache_wait(struct inode *inode)
> >         struct fuse_inode *fi = get_fuse_inode(inode);
> >
> >         return S_ISREG(inode->i_mode) &&
> > -               READ_ONCE(fi->iocachectr) < 0 && !fuse_inode_backing(fi);
> > +               READ_ONCE(fi->iocachectr) < 0 &&
> > +               !fuse_passthrough_op(inode, FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_RW_OPS);
> >  }
>
> Obviously, this was naive and not close to enough, because
> fuse_inode_set_passthrough() still takes the negative iocachectr
> refcount.
>
> Please ignore this. Supporting caching iomode and GETATTR
> passthrough is left for a future exercise, if anyone is ever interested.

Sounds good, I will continue to leave this unsupported for now.

Thanks for reviewing these patches.
>
> Thanks,
> Amir.

On Sat, May 16, 2026 at 9:57 AM Amir Goldstein <amir73il@gmail.com> wrote:

> On Sat, May 16, 2026 at 2:52 AM Joanne Koong <joannelkoong@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> > Servers can now pass through only reads or writes instead of being
> > required to pass through both. When the read or write operation is not
> > passed through, fall back to direct io for handling it. This avoids
> > cache coherency issues from mixing the backing file's page cache with
> > the fuse inode's page cache.
> >
> > Reject mmap when passthrough is partial or not set for read/writes since
> > mmap requires both read and write access to the backing page cache.
> >
> > The FOPEN_DIRECT_IO check in the read/write fallback is not strictly
> > needed as the caller already handles it, but including it here makes
> > the fallback logic self-contained.

> static inline u64 fuse_passthrough_op(struct inode *inode, u64 op_mask)
> {
>         struct fuse_inode *fi = get_fuse_inode(inode);
>         struct fuse_backing *fb = fuse_inode_passthrough(fi);
>
>         return !fb ? 0 : fb->ops_mask & op_mask;
> }
>
> static inline struct file *fuse_file_passthrough_op(struct file *file,
>                                                     u64 op_mask)
> {
>         struct fuse_file *ff = file->private_data;
>
>         /*
>          * FOPEN_DIRECT_IO can be used to opt-out of passthrough per file and
>          * ops_mask can be used to opt-out of passthrough per operation type.
>          */
>         return fuse_file_passthrough(ff) &&
>                 !(ff->open_flags & FOPEN_DIRECT_IO) &&
>                 fuse_passthrough_op(file_inode(file), op_mask) == op_mask;
> }
>
> ...
>
> static ssize_t fuse_splice_write(struct pipe_inode_info *pipe, struct file *out,
>                                  loff_t *ppos, size_t len, unsigned int flags)
> {
>         if (fuse_file_passthrough_op(out, FUSE_PASSTHROUGH_OP_WRITE))
>                 return fuse_passthrough_splice_write(pipe, out, ppos,
